   Strategy: ATR‑Band Mean Reversion (Sideways Volatility)
   Rationale: In a sideways market with ≈30% vol, price tends to oscillate around a stable range. Using ATR‑based price bands captures short‐term swings while limiting downside. Overall, the strategy exploits the range and high vol without committing to directional bets.
   Actions: 1️⃣ Define a 5‑day ATR on the base instrument and calculate a lower band at ‑0.5 ATR and an upper band at +0.5 ATR., 2️⃣ When price falls below the lower band, buy a 5‑day ATM option (call if bullish bias, put if bearish) and simultaneously place a 5‑day stop‑loss at 1 ATR below entry., 3️⃣ When price rises above the upper band, sell the same‑sized ATM option (short) and set a 5‑day stop‑loss at 1 ATR above exit., 4️⃣ Use the 25 % cash allocation to buy a weekly option ladder: short 1‑5 day OTM calls and puts on the same contract to capture time decay while keeping the delta neutral., 5️⃣ Adjust the 25 % allocation quarterly – reinvest accrued premiums into new 5‑day strikes if the ATR remains high; otherwise reduce position size., 6️⃣ Monitor volume and implied volatility – adjust stop‑losses to 1½ ATR during spikes or tighten to 0.75 ATR if volatility drops below 20 %.

  Description: Check for items that need reordering

  Conditions: 2
